     <p>
      An
      <b>
       electric vehicle
      </b>
      (
      <b>
       EV
      </b>
      ), also referred to as an
      <b>
       electric drive vehicle
      </b>
      , uses one or more
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">
       electric motors
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Traction_motor" title="Traction motor">
       traction motors
      </a>
      for propulsion. An electric vehicle may be powered through a collector system by electricity from off-vehicle sources, or may be self-contained with a battery or generator to convert fuel to electricity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        [1]
       </a>
      </sup>
      EVs include road and rail vehicles, surface and underwater vessels,
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_aircraft" title="Electric aircraft">
       electric aircraft
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Electrically_powered_spacecraft_propulsion" title="Electrically powered spacecraft propulsion">
       electric spacecraft
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      EVs first came into existence in the mid-19th century, when electricity was among the preferred methods for motor vehicle propulsion, providing a level of comfort and ease of operation that could not be achieved by the gasoline cars of the time. The internal combustion engine (ICE) has been the dominant propulsion method for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">
       motor vehicles
      </a>
      for almost 100 years, but electric power has remained commonplace in other vehicle types, such as trains and smaller vehicles of all types.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_electric_vehicle" title="History of the electric vehicle">
       History of the electric vehicle
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="349" data-file-width="441" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg/220px-EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg/330px-EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg/440px-EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EdisonElectricCar1913.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">
         Edison
        </a>
        and a 1914
        <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Electric" title="Detroit Electric">
         Detroit Electric
        </a>
        model 47 (courtesy of the
        <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_American_History" title="National Museum of American History">
         National Museum of American History
        </a>
        )
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="590" data-file-width="1035" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg/220px-Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg/330px-Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg/440px-Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Electric_car_and_antique_car_on_display_at_1912_auto_show.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        An EV and an antique car on display at a 1912 auto show
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Electric motive power started in 1827, when Slovak-Hungarian priest
      <a href="/wiki/%C3%81nyos_Jedlik" title="Ányos Jedlik">
       Ányos Jedlik
      </a>
      built the first crude but viable electric motor, provided with stator, rotor and commutator, and the year after he used it to power a tiny car.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-2">
        [2]
       </a>
      </sup>
      A few years later, in 1835, professor
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sibrandus_Stratingh&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sibrandus Stratingh (page does not exist)">
       Sibrandus Stratingh
      </a>
      of University of Groningen, the Netherlands, built a small scale electric car and a Robert Anderson of Scotland is reported to have made a crude electric carriage sometime between the years of 1832 and 1839. Around the same period, early experimental electrical cars were moving on rails, too. American blacksmith and inventor
      <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Davenport_(inventor)" title="Thomas Davenport (inventor)">
       Thomas Davenport
      </a>
      built a toy electric locomotive, powered by a primitive electric motor, in 1835. In 1838, a Scotsman named
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Davidson_(inventor)" title="Robert Davidson (inventor)">
       Robert Davidson
      </a>
      built an electric locomotive that attained a speed of four miles per hour (6 km/h). In England a patent was granted in 1840 for the use of rails as conductors of electric current, and similar American patents were issued to
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lilley_and_Colten&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lilley and Colten (page does not exist)">
       Lilley and Colten
      </a>
      in 1847.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        [3]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Between 1832 and 1839 (the exact year is uncertain),
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Anderson_(inventor)" title="Robert Anderson (inventor)">
       Robert Anderson
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">
       Scotland
      </a>
      invented the first crude electric carriage, powered by non-rechargeable
      <a href="/wiki/Primary_cell" title="Primary cell">
       primary cells
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        [4]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      By the 20th century,
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">
       electric cars
      </a>
      and rail transport were commonplace, with commercial electric automobiles having the majority of the market. Over time their general-purpose commercial use reduced to specialist roles, as
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_platform_truck" title="Electric platform truck">
       platform trucks
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forklift_truck" title="Forklift truck">
       forklift trucks
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ambulance" title="Ambulance">
       ambulances
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        [5]
       </a>
      </sup>
      tow tractors and urban delivery vehicles, such as the iconic British
      <a href="/wiki/Milk_float" title="Milk float">
       milk float
      </a>
      ; for most of the 20th century, the UK was the world's largest user of electric road vehicles.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        [6]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Electrified trains were used for
      <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">
       coal
      </a>
      transport, as the motors did not use precious
      <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">
       oxygen
      </a>
      in the mines. Switzerland's lack of natural fossil resources forced the rapid electrification of
      <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Switzerland" title="Rail transport in Switzerland">
       their rail network
      </a>
      . One of the earliest
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rechargeable_batteries" title="Rechargeable batteries">
       rechargeable batteries
      </a>
      - the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nickel-iron_battery" title="Nickel-iron battery">
       nickel-iron battery
      </a>
      - was favored by
      <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">
       Edison
      </a>
      for use in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_cars" title="Electric cars">
       electric cars
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      EVs were among the earliest automobiles, and before the preeminence of light, powerful
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engines" title="Internal combustion engines">
       internal combustion engines
      </a>
      , electric automobiles held many vehicle land speed and distance records in the early 1900s. They were produced by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baker_Electric" title="Baker Electric">
       Baker Electric
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbia_Automobile_Company" title="Columbia Automobile Company">
       Columbia Electric
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Electric" title="Detroit Electric">
       Detroit Electric
      </a>
      , and others, and at one point in history out-sold gasoline-powered vehicles. In fact, in 1900, 28 percent of the cars on the road in the USA were electric. EVs were so popular that even President
      <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">
       Woodrow Wilson
      </a>
      and his secret service agents toured Washington DC in their Milburn Electrics, which covered 60–70 mi (100–110 km) per charge.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        [7]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      A number of developments contributed to decline of electric cars.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        [8]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Auto_trail" title="Auto trail">
       Improved road infrastructure
      </a>
      required a greater range than that offered by electric cars, and the discovery of large reserves of petroleum in Texas, Oklahoma, and California led to the wide availability of affordable gasoline/petrol, making internal combustion powered cars cheaper to operate over long distances.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Britannica-9">
        [9]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Also internal combustion powered cars became ever easier to operate thanks to the invention of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_starter" title="Electric starter">
       electric starter
      </a>
      by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Kettering" title="Charles Kettering">
       Charles Kettering
      </a>
      in 1912,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-R1_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-R1-10">
        [10]
       </a>
      </sup>
      which eliminated the need of a hand crank for starting a gasoline engine, and the noise emitted by ICE cars became more bearable thanks to the use of the
      <a href="/wiki/Muffler" title="Muffler">
       muffler
      </a>
      , which
      <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Percy_Maxim" title="Hiram Percy Maxim">
       Hiram Percy Maxim
      </a>
      had invented in 1897. As roads were improved outside urban areas electric vehicle range could not compete with the ICE. Finally,
      <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">
       the initiation of mass production
      </a>
      of gasoline-powered vehicles by
      <a href="/wiki/Henry_Ford" title="Henry Ford">
       Henry Ford
      </a>
      in 1913 reduced significantly the cost of gasoline cars as compared to electric cars.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aboutcom_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-aboutcom-11">
        [11]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the 1930s,
      <a href="/wiki/National_City_Lines" title="National City Lines">
       National City Lines
      </a>
      , which was a partnership of
      <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">
       General Motors
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Firestone_Tire_and_Rubber_Company" title="Firestone Tire and Rubber Company">
       Firestone
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_of_California" title="Standard Oil of California">
       Standard Oil of California
      </a>
      purchased many electric
      <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">
       tram
      </a>
      networks across the country to dismantle them and replace them with GM buses. The partnership was convicted of
      <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_streetcar_conspiracy" title="General Motors streetcar conspiracy">
       conspiring
      </a>
      to monopolize the sale of equipment and supplies to their subsidiary companies, but were acquitted of conspiring to monopolize the provision of transportation services.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Experimentation">
       Experimentation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Experimentation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In January 1990, General Motors' President introduced its EV concept two-seater, the "Impact", at the Los Angeles Auto Show. That September, the California Air Resources Board mandated major-automaker sales of EVs, in phases starting in 1998. From 1996 to 1998 GM produced 1117 EV1s, 800 of which were made available through three-year leases.
     </p>
     <p>
      Chrysler, Ford, GM, Honda, Nissan and Toyota also produced limited numbers of EVs for California drivers. In 2003, upon the expiration of GM's
      <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_EV1" title="General Motors EV1">
       EV1
      </a>
      leases, GM crushed them. The crushing has variously been attributed to:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       the auto industry's successful
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_federal_courts" title="United States federal courts">
        federal court
       </a>
       challenge to California's
       <a href="/wiki/Zero-emissions_vehicle" title="Zero-emissions vehicle">
        zero-emissions vehicle
       </a>
       mandate,
      </li>
      <li>
       a federal regulation requiring GM to produce and maintain spare parts for the few thousands EV1s and
      </li>
      <li>
       the success of the oil and auto industries' media campaign to reduce public acceptance of EVs.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EV1A014_(1)_cropped.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="782" data-file-width="1173" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg/220px-EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg/330px-EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg/440px-EV1A014_%281%29_cropped.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EV1A014_(1)_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/General_Motors_EV1" title="General Motors EV1">
         General Motors EV1
        </a>
        electric car (1996-1998), story told in movie
        <a href="/wiki/Who_Killed_the_Electric_Car%3F" title="Who Killed the Electric Car?">
         Who Killed the Electric Car?
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      A movie made on the subject in 2005-2006 was titled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Who_Killed_the_Electric_Car%3F" title="Who Killed the Electric Car?">
        Who Killed the Electric Car?
       </a>
      </i>
      and released theatrically by
      <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Classics" title="Sony Pictures Classics">
       Sony Pictures Classics
      </a>
      in 2006. The film explores the roles of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile_manufacturer" title="Automobile manufacturer">
       automobile manufacturers
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_industry" title="Oil industry">
       oil industry
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">
       U.S. government
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Battery_(electricity)" title="Battery (electricity)">
       batteries
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydrogen_(car)" title="Hydrogen (car)">
       hydrogen vehicles
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Consumer" title="Consumer">
       consumers
      </a>
      , and each of their roles in limiting the deployment and adoption of this technology.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ford" title="Ford">
       Ford
      </a>
      released a number of their
      <a href="/wiki/Ford_Ecostar" title="Ford Ecostar">
       Ford Ecostar
      </a>
      delivery vans into the market. Honda, Nissan and Toyota also repossessed and crushed most of their EVs, which, like the GM EV1s, had been available only by closed-end lease. After public protests, Toyota sold 200 of its
      <a href="/wiki/Toyota_RAV4_EV" title="Toyota RAV4 EV">
       RAV EVs
      </a>
      to eager buyers; they later sold at over their original forty-thousand-dollar price. This lesson did not go unlearned;
      <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">
       BMW
      </a>
      of Canada sold off a number of Mini EV's when their Canadian testing ended.
     </p>
     <p>
      The production of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_Berlingo_Electrique" title="Citroën Berlingo Electrique">
       Citroën Berlingo Electrique
      </a>
      stopped in September 2005.
     </p>
     <div style="clear:both;">
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Reintroduction">
       Reintroduction
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Reintroduction">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      During the last few decades,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_with_petroleum" title="Environmental issues with petroleum">
       environmental impact
      </a>
      of the petroleum-based transportation infrastructure, along with the fear of
      <a href="/wiki/Peak_oil" title="Peak oil">
       peak oil
      </a>
      , has led to renewed interest in an electric transportation infrastructure.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSC_12-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-RSC-12">
        [12]
       </a>
      </sup>
      EVs differ from
      <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">
       fossil fuel
      </a>
      -powered vehicles in that the electricity they consume can be generated from a wide range of sources, including fossil fuels,
      <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">
       nuclear power
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">
       renewable
      </a>
      sources such as
      <a href="/wiki/Tidal_power" title="Tidal power">
       tidal power
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">
       solar power
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">
       wind power
      </a>
      or any combination of those. The
      <a href="/wiki/Carbon_footprint" title="Carbon footprint">
       carbon footprint
      </a>
      and other emissions of electric vehicles varies depending on the fuel and technology used for
      <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">
       electricity generation
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        [13]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        [14]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The electricity may then be stored on board the vehicle using a
      <a href="/wiki/Battery_(electricity)" title="Battery (electricity)">
       battery
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Flywheel_energy_storage" title="Flywheel energy storage">
       flywheel
      </a>
      , or
      <a href="/wiki/Supercapacitor" title="Supercapacitor">
       supercapacitors
      </a>
      . Vehicles making use of engines working on the principle of
      <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">
       combustion
      </a>
      can usually only derive their energy from a single or a few sources, usually non-renewable fossil fuels. A key advantage of hybrid or plug-in electric vehicles is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking">
       regenerative braking
      </a>
      due to their capability to recover energy normally lost during braking as electricity is stored in the on-board battery.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:277px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nissan_Leaf_and_Tesla_Model_S_in_Norway_cropped.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="3755" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nissan_Leaf_and_Tesla_Model_S_in_Norway_cropped.jpg/275px-Nissan_Leaf_and_Tesla_Model_S_in_Norway_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nissan_Leaf_and_Tesla_Model_S_in_Norway_cropped.jpg/413px-Nissan_Leaf_and_Tesla_Model_S_in_Norway_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Nissan_Leaf_and_Tesla_Model_S_in_Norway_cropped.jpg/550px-Nissan_Leaf_and_Tesla_Model_S_in_Norway_cropped.jpg 2x" width="275"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nissan_Leaf_and_Tesla_Model_S_in_Norway_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The world's two best selling all-electric cars of all-time are the
        <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">
         Nissan Leaf
        </a>
        (left), with global sales of 200,000 units, and the
        <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">
         Tesla Model S
        </a>
        (right), with about 100,000 units, both, as of early December 2015.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopPEVs112015_15-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-TopPEVs112015-15">
          [15]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      As of September 2014
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Series_production" title="Series production">
       series production
      </a>
      highway-capable
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All-electric_car" title="All-electric car">
       all-electric cars
      </a>
      available in some countries for retail customers include the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_i_MiEV" title="Mitsubishi i MiEV">
       Mitsubishi i MiEV
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chery_QQ3_EV" title="Chery QQ3 EV">
       Chery QQ3 EV
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JAC_J3_EV" title="JAC J3 EV">
       JAC J3 EV
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">
       Nissan Leaf
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Smart_ED" title="Smart ED">
       Smart ED
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/BYD_e6" title="BYD e6">
       BYD e6
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Bollor%C3%A9_Bluecar" title="Bolloré Bluecar">
       Bolloré Bluecar
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Renault_Fluence_Z.E." title="Renault Fluence Z.E.">
       Renault Fluence Z.E.
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ford_Focus_Electric" title="Ford Focus Electric">
       Ford Focus Electric
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">
       Tesla Model S
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honda_Fit_EV" title="Honda Fit EV">
       Honda Fit EV
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_RAV4_EV_Concept" title="Toyota RAV4 EV Concept">
       RAV4 EV second generation
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Renault_Zoe" title="Renault Zoe">
       Renault Zoe
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Roewe_E50" title="Roewe E50">
       Roewe E50
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Mahindra_e2o" title="Mahindra e2o">
       Mahindra e2o
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Spark_EV" title="Chevrolet Spark EV">
       Chevrolet Spark EV
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_SLS_AMG_Electric_Drive" title="Mercedes-Benz SLS AMG Electric Drive">
       Mercedes-Benz SLS AMG Electric Drive
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Fiat_500" title="Fiat 500">
       Fiat 500
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volkswagen_e-Up!" title="Volkswagen e-Up!">
       Volkswagen e-Up!
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/BMW_i3" title="BMW i3">
       BMW i3
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Kia_Soul_EV" title="Kia Soul EV">
       Kia Soul EV
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Volkswagen_e-Golf" title="Volkswagen e-Golf">
       Volkswagen e-Golf
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_B-Class_Electric_Drive" title="Mercedes-Benz B-Class Electric Drive">
       Mercedes-Benz B-Class Electric Drive
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venucia_e30" title="Venucia e30">
       Venucia e30
      </a>
      . As of early December 2015, the Leaf, with 200,000 units sold worldwide, is the world's top-selling highway-capable all-electric car in history, followed by the
      <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">
       Tesla Model S
      </a>
      with global deliveries of about 100,000 units.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TopPEVs112015_15-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-TopPEVs112015-15">
        [15]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of May 2015
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , more than 500,000 highway-capable all-electric passenger cars and light utility vehicles have been sold worldwide since 2008, out of total global sales of about 850,000 light-duty
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">
       plug-in electric vehicles
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GlobalEV052015_16-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GlobalEV052015-16">
        [16]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global850K_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Global850K-17">
        [17]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of May 2015
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , the United States continued to have the largest fleet of highway-capable plug-in electric vehicles in the world, with about 335,000 highway legal
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_car" title="Plug-in electric car">
       plug-in electric cars
      </a>
      sold in the country since 2008, and representing about 40% of the global stock.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global700K_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Global700K-18">
        [18]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales052015US_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Sales052015US-19">
        [19]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
       California
      </a>
      is the largest plug-in car regional market in the country, with almost 143,000 units sold between December 2010 and March 2015, representing over 46% of all plug-in cars sold in the U.S.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cal2014_20-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Cal2014-20">
        [20]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calif100K_21-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Calif100K-21">
        [21]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calif4Q2014_22-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Calif4Q2014-22">
        [22]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Calif1Q2015_23-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Calif1Q2015-23">
        [23]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Norway is the country with the highest
      <a href="/wiki/Market_penetration" title="Market penetration">
       market penetration
      </a>
      per capita in the world, with four plug-in electric vehicles per 1000 inhabitants in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top6Global2013_24-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Top6Global2013-24">
        [24]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In March 2014, Norway became the first country where over 1 in every 100 passenger cars on the roads is a plug-in electric.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NorwayEVSales032014_25-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NorwayEVSales032014-25">
        [25]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        [26]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Norway also has the world's largest plug-in electric segment market share of total new car sales, 13.8% in 2014, up from 5.6% in 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global700K_18-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Global700K-18">
        [18]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NorwayEVSales2013_27-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NorwayEVSales2013-27">
        [27]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In June 2016,
      <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">
       Andorra
      </a>
      became the second country in this list, with a 6% of market share combining electric vehicles and
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">
       plug-in hybrids
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        [28]
       </a>
      </sup>
      due to a strong public policy providing multiple advantages.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        [29]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of May 2015
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , there were 58,989 plug-in electric vehicles registered in Norway, consisting of 54,160 all-electric vehicles and 4,829 plug-in hybrids.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NorwayStat_30-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NorwayStat-30">
        [30]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Electricity_sources">
       Electricity sources
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Electricity sources">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      There are many ways to generate electricity, of varying costs, efficiency and ecological desirability.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:229px;max-width:229px">
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:227px;max-width:227px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG/225px-2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG/338px-2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG/450px-2402_%27County_of_Hampshire%27_at_Wool.JPG 2x" width="225"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         A passenger train, taking power through a
         <a href="/wiki/Third_rail" title="Third rail">
          third rail
         </a>
         with return through the traction rails
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:227px;max-width:227px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SwissMGB.jpg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="765" data-file-width="1024" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/SwissMGB.jpg/225px-SwissMGB.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/SwissMGB.jpg/338px-SwissMGB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/SwissMGB.jpg/450px-SwissMGB.jpg 2x" width="225"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         An
         <a href="/wiki/Electric_locomotive" title="Electric locomotive">
          electric locomotive
         </a>
         at
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brig,_Switzerland" title="Brig, Switzerland">
          Brig
         </a>
         , Switzerland
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:227px;max-width:227px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Electric_Bus_in_Santa_Barbara_California.JPG">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Electric_Bus_in_Santa_Barbara_California.JPG/225px-Electric_Bus_in_Santa_Barbara_California.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Electric_Bus_in_Santa_Barbara_California.JPG/338px-Electric_Bus_in_Santa_Barbara_California.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Electric_Bus_in_Santa_Barbara_California.JPG/450px-Electric_Bus_in_Santa_Barbara_California.JPG 2x" width="225"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         <a href="/wiki/Electric_bus" title="Electric bus">
          Electric bus
         </a>
         in Santa Barbara, California
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Connection_to_generator_plants">
       Connection to generator plants
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Connection to generator plants">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       direct connection to generation plants as is common among
       <a href="/wiki/Electric_locomotive" title="Electric locomotive">
        electric trains
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">
        trolley buses
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Trolleytruck" title="Trolleytruck">
        trolley trucks
       </a>
       (See also :
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overhead_lines" title="Overhead lines">
        overhead lines
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Third_rail" title="Third rail">
        third rail
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Conduit_current_collection" title="Conduit current collection">
        conduit current collection
       </a>
       )
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Online_Electric_Vehicle" title="Online Electric Vehicle">
        Online Electric Vehicle
       </a>
       collects power from electric power strips buried under the road surface through
       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_induction" title="Electromagnetic induction">
        electromagnetic induction
       </a>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Onboard_generators_and_hybrid_EVs">
       Onboard generators and hybrid EVs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Onboard generators and hybrid EVs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      (See articles on
      <a href="/wiki/Diesel-electric_transmission" title="Diesel-electric transmission">
       diesel-electric
      </a>
      and gasoline-electric
      <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">
       hybrid
      </a>
      locomotion for information on EVs using also
      <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">
       combustion engines
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       generated on-board using a diesel engine:
       <a href="/wiki/Diesel-electric_transmission" title="Diesel-electric transmission">
        diesel-electric
       </a>
       locomotive
      </li>
      <li>
       generated on-board using a
       <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">
        fuel cell
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell_vehicle" title="Fuel cell vehicle">
        fuel cell vehicle
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       generated on-board using
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">
        nuclear energy
       </a>
       : nuclear
       <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">
        submarines
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">
        aircraft carriers
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       renewable sources such as
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">
        solar power
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_vehicle" title="Solar vehicle">
        solar vehicle
       </a>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      It is also possible to have hybrid EVs that derive electricity from multiple sources. Such as:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       on-board
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rechargeable_electricity_storage_system&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rechargeable electricity storage system (page does not exist)">
        rechargeable electricity storage system
       </a>
       (RESS) and a direct continuous connection to land-based generation plants for purposes of on-highway recharging with unrestricted highway range
      </li>
      <li>
       on-board rechargeable electricity storage system and a fueled propulsion power source (
       <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">
        internal combustion engine
       </a>
       ):
       <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">
        plug-in hybrid
       </a>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      Another form of chemical to electrical conversion is
      <a href="/wiki/Fuel_cell" title="Fuel cell">
       fuel cells
      </a>
      , projected for future use.
     </p>
     <p>
      For especially large EVs, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">
       submarines
      </a>
      , the chemical energy of the diesel-electric can be replaced by a
      <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">
       nuclear reactor
      </a>
      . The nuclear reactor usually provides heat, which drives a
      <a href="/wiki/Steam_turbine" title="Steam turbine">
       steam turbine
      </a>
      , which drives a generator, which is then fed to the propulsion.
      <i>
       See
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuclear_Power" title="Nuclear Power">
        Nuclear Power
       </a>
      </i>
     </p>
     <p>
      A few experimental vehicles, such as some cars and a handful of aircraft use
      <a href="/wiki/Solar_panel" title="Solar panel">
       solar panels
      </a>
      for electricity.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Onboard_storage">
       Onboard storage
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Onboard storage">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      These systems are powered from an external generator plant (nearly always when stationary), and then disconnected before motion occurs, and the electricity is stored in the vehicle until needed.
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       on-board
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rechargeable_electricity_storage_system&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rechargeable electricity storage system (page does not exist)">
        rechargeable electricity storage system
       </a>
       (RESS), called Full Electric Vehicles (FEV). Power storage methods include:
       <ul>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Chemical_energy" title="Chemical energy">
          chemical energy
         </a>
         stored on the vehicle in on-board batteries:
         <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">
          Battery electric vehicle
         </a>
         (BEV)
        </li>
        <li>
         kinetic energy storage:
         <a href="/wiki/Gyrobus" title="Gyrobus">
          flywheels
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         static
         <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">
          energy
         </a>
         stored on the vehicle in on-board
         <a href="/wiki/Electric_double-layer_capacitor" title="Electric double-layer capacitor">
          electric double-layer capacitors
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Battery_(electricity)" title="Battery (electricity)">
       Batteries
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_double-layer_capacitor" title="Electric double-layer capacitor">
       electric double-layer capacitors
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Flywheel_energy_storage" title="Flywheel energy storage">
       flywheel energy storage
      </a>
      are forms of rechargeable on-board
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Rechargeable_electricity_storage_system&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Rechargeable electricity storage system (page does not exist)">
       electrical storage
      </a>
      . By avoiding an intermediate mechanical step, the
      <a href="/wiki/Energy_conversion_efficiency" title="Energy conversion efficiency">
       energy conversion efficiency
      </a>
      can be improved over the hybrids already discussed, by avoiding unnecessary energy conversions. Furthermore, electro-chemical batteries conversions are easy to reverse, allowing electrical energy to be stored in chemical form.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Lithium-ion_battery">
       Lithium-ion battery
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Lithium-ion battery">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ASEAG_999_Seite.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="4352" height="101" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/ASEAG_999_Seite.jpg/220px-ASEAG_999_Seite.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/ASEAG_999_Seite.jpg/330px-ASEAG_999_Seite.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/ASEAG_999_Seite.jpg/440px-ASEAG_999_Seite.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ASEAG_999_Seite.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_bus" title="Battery electric bus">
         Battery electric bus
        </a>
        powered with lithium-ion batteries
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3282" data-file-width="4923" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg/220px-Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg/330px-Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg/440px-Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Iveco_Stralis_AD_190_E-truck._Lidl._Spielvogel.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Electric_truck" title="Electric truck">
         Electric truck
        </a>
        e-Force One
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery" title="Electric vehicle battery">
       Electric vehicle battery
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Most electric vehicles use
      <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery" title="Lithium-ion battery">
       lithium ion batteries
      </a>
      . Lithium ion batteries have higher
      <a href="/wiki/Energy_density" title="Energy density">
       energy density
      </a>
      , longer
      <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery#Lifespan_and_cycle_stability" title="Rechargeable battery">
       life span
      </a>
      and higher
      <a href="/wiki/Power_density" title="Power density">
       power density
      </a>
      than most other practical batteries. Complicating factors include safety, durability, thermal breakdown and
      <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery#Price_history" title="Rechargeable battery">
       cost
      </a>
      . Li-ion batteries should be used within safe temperature and voltage ranges in order to operate safely and efficiently.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        [31]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Increasing the battery's lifespan decreases effective costs. One technique is to operate a subset of the battery cells at a time and switching these subsets.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        [32]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_motor">
       Electric motor
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Electric motor">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Traction_motor" title="Traction motor">
       Traction motor
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Energy_conversion_efficiency" title="Energy conversion efficiency">
       Energy conversion efficiency
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The power of a vehicle electric motor, as in other vehicles, is measured in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kilowatt" title="Kilowatt">
       kilowatts
      </a>
      (kW). 100 kW is roughly equivalent to 134
      <a href="/wiki/Horsepower" title="Horsepower">
       horsepower
      </a>
      , although electric motors can deliver their full torque over a wide RPM range, so the performance is not equivalent, and far exceeds a 134 horsepower (100 kW) fuel-powered motor, which has a limited torque curve.
     </p>
     <p>
      Usually,
      <a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">
       direct current
      </a>
      (DC) electricity is fed into a DC/AC inverter where it is converted to
      <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">
       alternating current
      </a>
      (AC) electricity and this AC electricity is connected to a 3-phase AC motor.
     </p>
     <p>
      For electric trains,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forklift_truck" title="Forklift truck">
       forklift trucks
      </a>
      , and some electric cars, DC motors are often used. In some cases,
      <a href="/wiki/Universal_motor" title="Universal motor">
       universal motors
      </a>
      are used, and then AC or DC may be employed. In recent production vehicles, various motor types have been implemented, for instance:
      <a href="/wiki/Induction_motor" title="Induction motor">
       Induction motors
      </a>
      within Tesla Motor vehicles and permanent magnet machines in the Nissan Leaf.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        [33]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Vehicle_types">
       Vehicle types
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Vehicle types">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Volt_charging_station.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Volt_charging_station.jpg/280px-Volt_charging_station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Volt_charging_station.jpg/420px-Volt_charging_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Volt_charging_station.jpg/560px-Volt_charging_station.jpg 2x" width="280"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Volt_charging_station.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">
         Chevrolet Volt
        </a>
        is the world's top selling
        <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">
         plug-in hybrid
        </a>
        of all time. Global Volt/Ampera family sales passed the 100,000 unit milestone in October 2015.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Volt100K_34-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Volt100K-34">
          [34]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      It is generally possible to equip any kind of vehicle with an electric powertrain.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_vehicles">
       Ground vehicles
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ground vehicles">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Plug-in_electric_vehicle">
       Plug-in electric vehicle
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Plug-in electric vehicle">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">
       Plug-in electric vehicle
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">
       Plug-in hybrid
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">
       electric car
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      A plug-in electric vehicle (PEV) is any
      <a href="/wiki/Motor_vehicle" title="Motor vehicle">
       motor vehicle
      </a>
      that can be recharged from any external source of electricity, such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wall_socket" title="Wall socket">
       wall sockets
      </a>
      , and the electricity stored in the
      <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery" title="Rechargeable battery">
       rechargeable battery packs
      </a>
      drives or contributes to drive the wheels. PEV is a subcategory of electric vehicles that includes
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All-electric_vehicle" title="All-electric vehicle">
       all-electric or battery electric vehicles
      </a>
      (BEVs),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid_vehicle" title="Plug-in hybrid vehicle">
       plug-in hybrid vehicles
      </a>
      , (PHEVs), and
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_conversion" title="Electric vehicle conversion">
       electric vehicle conversions
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">
       hybrid electric vehicles
      </a>
      and conventional
      <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">
       internal combustion engine
      </a>
      vehicles.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PEVs_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PEVs-35">
        [35]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSE_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CSE-36">
        [36]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        [37]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cumulative global sales totaled over 1.5 million plug-in cars and utility vans by the end of May 2016.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global1.5mi_38-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Global1.5mi-38">
        [38]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of June 2016
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , the world's top selling plug-in electric cars are the
      <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Leaf" title="Nissan Leaf">
       Nissan Leaf
      </a>
      , with global sales of more than 228,000 units, followed by the all-electric
      <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">
       Tesla Model S
      </a>
      with about 129,400 units sold worldwide, the
      <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Volt" title="Chevrolet Volt">
       Chevrolet Volt
      </a>
      plug-in hybrid, which together with its sibling the Opel/Vauxhall Ampera has combined global sales of about 117,300 units, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mitsubishi_Outlander_P-HEV" title="Mitsubishi Outlander P-HEV">
       Mitsubishi Outlander P-HEV
      </a>
      with about 107,400 units, and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prius_Plug-in_Hybrid" title="Prius Plug-in Hybrid">
       Prius Plug-in Hybrid
      </a>
      with over 75,400 units.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top10Global062016_39-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Top10Global062016-39">
        [39]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Hybrid_EVs">
       Hybrid EVs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hybrid EVs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">
       Hybrid electric vehicle
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      A
      <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">
       hybrid electric vehicle
      </a>
      combines a conventional (usually fossil fuel-powered) powertrain with some form of electric propulsion. As of April 2016
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , over 11 million hybrid electric vehicles have been sold worldwide since their inception in 1997. Japan is the market leader with more than 5 million hybrids sold, followed by the United States with cumulative sales of over 4 million units since 1999, and Europe with about 1.5 million hybrids delivered since 2000.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US4mi_40-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-US4mi-40">
        [40]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Japan has the world's highest hybrid
      <a href="/wiki/Market_penetration" title="Market penetration">
       market penetration
      </a>
      . By 2013 the hybrid
      <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">
       market share
      </a>
      accounted for more than 30% of new standard passenger car sold, and about 20% new passenger vehicle sales including
      <a href="/wiki/Kei_car" title="Kei car">
       kei cars
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JapHEVshare_41-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-JapHEVshare-41">
        [41]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Norway ranks second with a hybrid market share of 6.9% of new car sales in 2014, followed by the Netherlands with 3.7%
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUpocketbook2014_42-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EUpocketbook2014-42">
        [42]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Global hybrid sales are by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Motor_Company" title="Toyota Motor Company">
       Toyota Motor Company
      </a>
      with more than 9 million
      <a href="/wiki/Lexus" title="Lexus">
       Lexus
      </a>
      and Toyota hybrids sold as of April 2016
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMC9miHEVs_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-TMC9miHEVs-43">
        [43]
       </a>
      </sup>
      followed by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Honda_Motor_Co.,_Ltd." title="Honda Motor Co., Ltd.">
       Honda Motor Co., Ltd.
      </a>
      with cumulative global sales of more than 1.35 million hybrids as of June 2014
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Honda1mi_44-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Honda1mi-44">
        [44]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Honda2013_45-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Honda2013-45">
        [45]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Honda062014_46-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Honda062014-46">
        [46]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Corporation" title="Ford Motor Corporation">
       Ford Motor Corporation
      </a>
      with over 424,000 hybrids sold in the United States through June 2015,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ford200K_47-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ford200K-47">
        [47]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2012US_48-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Sales2012US-48">
        [48]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2013US_49-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Sales2013US-49">
        [49]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales2014US_50-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Sales2014US-50">
        [50]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales062015US_51-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Sales062015US-51">
        [51]
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Group" title="Hyundai Group">
       Hyundai Group
      </a>
      with cumulative global sales of 200,000 hybrids as of March 2014
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , including both
      <a href="/wiki/Hyundai_Motor_Company" title="Hyundai Motor Company">
       Hyundai Motor Company
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Kia_Motors" title="Kia Motors">
       Kia Motors
      </a>
      hybrid models.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hyundai200K_52-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Hyundai200K-52">
        [52]
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of April 2016
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , worldwide hybrid sales are led by the
      <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Prius" title="Toyota Prius">
       Toyota Prius
      </a>
      liftback, with cumulative sales of over 3.7 million units. The Prius
      <a href="/wiki/Nameplate" title="Nameplate">
       nameplate
      </a>
      has sold more than 5.7 million hybrids up to April 2016.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PriusTop_53-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PriusTop-53">
        [53]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="On-_and_off-road_EVs">
       On- and off-road EVs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: On- and off-road EVs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Electric_powertrain.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="150" data-file-width="390" height="85" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Electric_powertrain.jpg/220px-Electric_powertrain.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Electric_powertrain.jpg/330px-Electric_powertrain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/Electric_powertrain.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Electric_powertrain.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        An electric powertrain used by
        <a href="/wiki/Power_Vehicle_Innovation" title="Power Vehicle Innovation">
         Power Vehicle Innovation
        </a>
        for
        <a href="/wiki/Truck" title="Truck">
         trucks
        </a>
        or
        <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">
         buses
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
         <a href="#cite_note-54">
          [54]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      EVs are on the road in many functions, including
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_cars" title="Electric cars">
       electric cars
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">
       electric trolleybuses
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_bus" title="Electric bus">
       electric buses
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_bus" title="Battery electric bus">
       battery electric buses
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_truck" title="Electric truck">
       electric trucks
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_bicycles" title="Electric bicycles">
       electric bicycles
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_motorcycles_and_scooters" title="Electric motorcycles and scooters">
       electric motorcycles and scooters
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neighborhood_electric_vehicles" title="Neighborhood electric vehicles">
       neighborhood electric vehicles
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Golf_cart" title="Golf cart">
       golf carts
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Milk_float" title="Milk float">
       milk floats
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forklift_truck" title="Forklift truck">
       forklifts
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Off-road_vehicle" title="Off-road vehicle">
       Off-road vehicles
      </a>
      include electrified
      <a href="/wiki/All-terrain_vehicle" title="All-terrain vehicle">
       all-terrain vehicles
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Elec-Trak" title="Elec-Trak">
       tractors
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Railborne_EVs">
       Railborne EVs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Railborne EVs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Railway_electrification_system" title="Railway electrification system">
       Railway electrification system
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="840" data-file-width="1131" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg/220px-2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg/330px-2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg/440px-2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2001-03-31.H-TW2000-Vahrenwalder-Platz.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Streetcar" title="Streetcar">
         streetcar
        </a>
        (or
        <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">
         Tram
        </a>
        ) drawing current from a single overhead wire through a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pantograph_(rail)" title="Pantograph (rail)">
         pantograph
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The fixed nature of a rail line makes it relatively easy to power EVs through permanent
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overhead_lines" title="Overhead lines">
       overhead lines
      </a>
      or electrified
      <a href="/wiki/Third_rail" title="Third rail">
       third rails
      </a>
      , eliminating the need for heavy onboard batteries.
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_locomotive" title="Electric locomotive">
       Electric locomotives
      </a>
      , electric
      <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">
       trams/streetcars/trolleys
      </a>
      , electric
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_rail_system" title="Light rail system">
       light rail systems
      </a>
      , and electric
      <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">
       rapid transit
      </a>
      are all in common use today, especially in Europe and Asia.
     </p>
     <p>
      Since electric trains do not need to carry a heavy internal combustion engine or large batteries, they can have very good
      <a href="/wiki/Power-to-weight_ratio" title="Power-to-weight ratio">
       power-to-weight ratios
      </a>
      . This allows
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_speed_train" title="High speed train">
       high speed trains
      </a>
      such as France's double-deck
      <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">
       TGVs
      </a>
      to operate at speeds of 320 km/h (200 mph) or higher, and
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_locomotive" title="Electric locomotive">
       electric locomotives
      </a>
      to have a much higher power output than
      <a href="/wiki/Diesel_locomotive" title="Diesel locomotive">
       diesel locomotives
      </a>
      . In addition, they have higher short-term
      <a href="/wiki/Overcurrent" title="Overcurrent">
       surge power
      </a>
      for fast acceleration, and using
      <a href="/wiki/Regenerative_brake" title="Regenerative brake">
       regenerative brakes
      </a>
      can put braking power back into the
      <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">
       electrical grid
      </a>
      rather than wasting it.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maglev_(transport)" title="Maglev (transport)">
       Maglev
      </a>
      trains are also nearly always EVs.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Space_rover_vehicles">
       Space rover vehicles
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Space rover vehicles">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Rover_(space_exploration)" title="Rover (space exploration)">
       Rover (space exploration)
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Manned and unmanned vehicles have been used to explore the
      <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">
       Moon
      </a>
      and other planets in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_system" title="Solar system">
       solar system
      </a>
      . On the last three missions of the
      <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">
       Apollo program
      </a>
      in 1971 and 1972, astronauts drove
      <a href="/wiki/Silver-oxide_battery" title="Silver-oxide battery">
       silver-oxide battery
      </a>
      -powered
      <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Roving_Vehicle" title="Lunar Roving Vehicle">
       Lunar Roving Vehicles
      </a>
      distances up to 35.7 kilometers (22.2 mi) on the lunar surface. Unmanned,
      <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaics" title="Photovoltaics">
       solar-powered
      </a>
      rovers have explored the Moon and
      <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">
       Mars
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Airborne_EVs">
       Airborne EVs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Airborne EVs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Since the beginning of the era of
      <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">
       aviation
      </a>
      , electric power for aircraft has received a great deal of experimentation. Currently flying
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_aircraft" title="Electric aircraft">
       electric aircraft
      </a>
      include manned and unmanned aerial vehicles.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Seaborne_EVs">
       Seaborne EVs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Seaborne EVs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Submarine#Propulsion" title="Submarine">
       Submarine § Propulsion
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ship#Propulsion_systems" title="Ship">
       Ship § Propulsion systems
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_boat" title="Electric boat">
       electric boat
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="572" data-file-width="400" height="315" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg/220px-Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg/330px-Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oceanvolt_sd8.6_electric_saildrive_motor.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Oceanvolt SD8.6 electric saildrive motor
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_boat" title="Electric boat">
       Electric boats
      </a>
      were popular around the turn of the 20th century. Interest in quiet and potentially renewable marine transportation has steadily increased since the late 20th century, as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_cells" title="Solar cells">
       solar cells
      </a>
      have given
      <a href="/wiki/Motorboat" title="Motorboat">
       motorboats
      </a>
      the infinite range of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sailboats" title="Sailboats">
       sailboats
      </a>
      . Electric motors can and have also been used in sailboats instead of traditional diesel engines.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        [55]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Electric ferries operate routinely.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        [56]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">
       Submarines
      </a>
      use batteries (charged by
      <a href="/wiki/Diesel-electric_transmission" title="Diesel-electric transmission">
       diesel
      </a>
      or gasoline engines at the surface),
      <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_submarine" title="Nuclear submarine">
       nuclear
      </a>
      power, fuel cells
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        [57]
       </a>
      </sup>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Stirling_engine" title="Stirling engine">
       Stirling engines
      </a>
      to run electric motor-driven propellers.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Electrically_powered_spacecraft">
       Electrically powered spacecraft
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Electrically powered spacecraft">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Electrically_powered_spacecraft_propulsion" title="Electrically powered spacecraft propulsion">
       Electrically powered spacecraft propulsion
      </a>
     </div>
