     <p>
      Electric power has a long history of use in
      <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">
       spacecraft
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ion_1964_58-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ion_1964-58">
        [58]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cybulski_59-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Cybulski-59">
        [59]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The power sources used for spacecraft are batteries, solar panels and nuclear power. Current methods of propelling a spacecraft with electricity include the
      <a href="/wiki/Arcjet_rocket" title="Arcjet rocket">
       arcjet rocket
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrostatic_ion_thruster" title="Electrostatic ion thruster">
       electrostatic ion thruster
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hall_effect_thruster" title="Hall effect thruster">
       Hall effect thruster
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Field_Emission_Electric_Propulsion" title="Field Emission Electric Propulsion">
       Field Emission Electric Propulsion
      </a>
      .
      <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft_propulsion#Table_of_methods" title="Spacecraft propulsion">
       A number of other methods have been proposed
      </a>
      , with varying levels of feasibility.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
         <span title="Statement needs to be more specific about the content to which it refers. (August 2014)">
          specify
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_and_motors">
       Energy and motors
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Energy and motors">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1620" data-file-width="2232" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG/220px-Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG/330px-Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG/440px-Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tr%C3%A5dbuss_Landskrona.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A
        <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">
         trolleybus
        </a>
        uses two overhead wires to provide electric current supply and return to the power source
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SwissElectricBus.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="765" data-file-width="1024" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/SwissElectricBus.jpg/220px-SwissElectricBus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/SwissElectricBus.jpg/330px-SwissElectricBus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/SwissElectricBus.jpg/440px-SwissElectricBus.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SwissElectricBus.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        An electric bus at
        <a href="/wiki/Lucerne" title="Lucerne">
         Lucerne
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arriva_3006-III.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2140" data-file-width="3268" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Arriva_3006-III.JPG/220px-Arriva_3006-III.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Arriva_3006-III.JPG/330px-Arriva_3006-III.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Arriva_3006-III.JPG/440px-Arriva_3006-III.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arriva_3006-III.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_bus" title="Battery electric bus">
         Battery electric bus
        </a>
        by
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BYD_electric_bus" title="BYD electric bus">
         BYD
        </a>
        in the Netherlands
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Most large electric transport systems are powered by stationary sources of electricity that are directly connected to the vehicles through wires. Electric traction allows the use of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking">
       regenerative braking
      </a>
      , in which the motors are used as brakes and become generators that transform the motion of, usually, a train into electrical power that is then fed back into the lines. This system is particularly advantageous in mountainous operations, as descending vehicles can produce a large portion of the power required for those ascending. This regenerative system is only viable if the system is large enough to utilise the power generated by descending vehicles.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the systems above motion is provided by a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rotary_motor" title="Rotary motor">
       rotary
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">
       electric motor
      </a>
      . However, it is possible to "unroll" the motor to drive directly against a special matched track. These
      <a href="/wiki/Linear_motor" title="Linear motor">
       linear motors
      </a>
      are used in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maglev_train" title="Maglev train">
       maglev trains
      </a>
      which float above the rails supported by
      <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_levitation" title="Magnetic levitation">
       magnetic levitation
      </a>
      . This allows for almost no rolling resistance of the vehicle and no mechanical wear and tear of the train or track. In addition to the high-performance control systems needed,
      <a href="/wiki/Railroad_switch" title="Railroad switch">
       switching
      </a>
      and curving of the tracks becomes difficult with linear motors, which to date has restricted their operations to high-speed point to point services.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Properties_of_EVs">
       Properties of EVs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Properties of EVs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Components">
       Components
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Components">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The type of
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery" title="Electric vehicle battery">
       battery
      </a>
      , the type of
      <a href="/wiki/Traction_motor" title="Traction motor">
       traction motor
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Motor_controller" title="Motor controller">
       motor controller
      </a>
      design vary according to the size, power and proposed application, which can be as small as a
      <a href="/wiki/Motorized_shopping_cart" title="Motorized shopping cart">
       motorized shopping cart
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Wheelchair" title="Wheelchair">
       wheelchair
      </a>
      , through
      <a href="/wiki/Pedelec" title="Pedelec">
       pedelecs
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_motorcycles_and_scooters" title="Electric motorcycles and scooters">
       electric motorcycles and scooters
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neighborhood_electric_vehicles" title="Neighborhood electric vehicles">
       neighborhood electric vehicles
      </a>
      , industrial
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fork-lift_truck" title="Fork-lift truck">
       fork-lift trucks
      </a>
      and including many
      <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_vehicle" title="Hybrid vehicle">
       hybrid vehicles
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_sources">
       Energy sources
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Energy sources">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Although EVs have few direct emissions, all rely on energy created through
      <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">
       electricity generation
      </a>
      , and will usually emit pollution and generate waste, unless it is generated by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_source" title="Renewable source">
       renewable source
      </a>
      power plants. Since EVs use whatever electricity is delivered by their electrical utility/grid operator, EVs can be made more or less efficient, polluting and expensive to run, by modifying the electrical generating stations. This would be done by an electrical utility under a government energy policy, in a timescale negotiated between utilities and government.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">
       Fossil fuel
      </a>
      vehicle efficiency and pollution standards take years to filter through a nation's fleet of vehicles. New efficiency and pollution standards rely on the purchase of new vehicles, often as the current vehicles already on the road reach their end-of-life. Only a few nations set a retirement age for old vehicles, such as Japan or
      <a href="/wiki/Driving_in_Singapore" title="Driving in Singapore">
       Singapore
      </a>
      , forcing periodic upgrading of all vehicles already on the road.
     </p>
     <p>
      EVs will take advantage of whatever environmental gains happen when a renewable energy generation station comes online, a
      <a href="/wiki/Fossil-fuel_power_station" title="Fossil-fuel power station">
       fossil-fuel power station
      </a>
      is decommissioned or upgraded. Conversely, if government policy or economic conditions shifts generators back to use more polluting fossil fuels and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine_vehicle" title="Internal combustion engine vehicle">
       internal combustion engine vehicles
      </a>
      (ICEVs), or more inefficient sources, the reverse can happen. Even in such a situation, electrical vehicles are still more efficient than a comparable amount of fossil fuel vehicles. In areas with a deregulated electrical energy market, an electrical vehicle owner can choose whether to run his electrical vehicle off conventional electrical energy sources, or strictly from renewable electrical energy sources (presumably at an additional cost), pushing other consumers onto conventional sources, and switch at any time between the two.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Issues_with_batteries">
       Issues with batteries
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Issues with batteries">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_battery" title="Electric vehicle battery">
       Electric vehicle battery
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Photo-CarBattery.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1515" data-file-width="1585" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Photo-CarBattery.jpg/220px-Photo-CarBattery.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Photo-CarBattery.jpg/330px-Photo-CarBattery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Photo-CarBattery.jpg/440px-Photo-CarBattery.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Photo-CarBattery.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Old: Banks of conventional lead-acid car batteries are still commonly used for EV propulsion
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="353" data-file-width="400" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg/220px-NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg/330px-NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b7/NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NASA_Lithium_Ion_Polymer_Battery.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        75 watt-hour/kilogram
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithium_ion_polymer_battery" title="Lithium ion polymer battery">
         lithium ion polymer battery
        </a>
        prototypes. Newer Li-poly cells provide up to 130 Wh/kg and last through thousands of charging cycles.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Efficiency">
       Efficiency
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Efficiency">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Because of the different methods of charging possible, the emissions produced have been quantified in different ways.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        [60]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Plug-in all-electric and hybrid vehicles also have different consumption characteristics.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-knipping_61-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-knipping-61">
        [61]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Electromagnetic_radiation">
       Electromagnetic radiation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Electromagnetic radiation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetic_radiation" title="Electromagnetic radiation">
       Electromagnetic radiation
      </a>
      from high performance electrical motors has been claimed to be associated with some human ailments, but such claims are largely unsubstantiated except for extremely high exposures.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        [62]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Electric motors can be shielded within a metallic
      <a href="/wiki/Faraday_cage" title="Faraday cage">
       Faraday cage
      </a>
      , but this reduces efficiency by adding weight to the vehicle, while it is not conclusive that all electromagnetic radiation can be contained.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Charging">
       Charging
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Charging">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Grid_capacity">
       Grid capacity
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Grid capacity">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      If a large proportion of private vehicles were to convert to grid electricity it would increase the demand for generation and transmission, and consequent emissions. However, overall energy consumption and emissions would diminish because of the higher efficiency of EVs over the entire cycle. In the USA it has been estimated there is already nearly sufficient existing power plant and transmission infrastructure, assuming that most charging would occur overnight, using the most efficient off-peak
      <a href="/wiki/Base_load" title="Base load">
       base load
      </a>
      sources.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_63-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-63">
        [63]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the UK however, things are different. While National Grid’s high-voltage electricity transmission system can currently manage the demand of 1 million electric cars, Steve Holliday (CEO National Grid PLC) said, “penetration up and above that becomes a real issue. Local distribution networks in cities like London may struggle to balance their grids if drivers choose to all plug in their cars at the same time."
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Charging_stations">
       Charging stations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Charging stations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BYD_Electric_Taxi.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1656" data-file-width="2892" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BYD_Electric_Taxi.jpg/220px-BYD_Electric_Taxi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BYD_Electric_Taxi.jpg/330px-BYD_Electric_Taxi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BYD_Electric_Taxi.jpg/440px-BYD_Electric_Taxi.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BYD_Electric_Taxi.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/BYD_e6" title="BYD e6">
         BYD e6
        </a>
        taxi in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shenzhen,_China" title="Shenzhen, China">
         Shenzhen, China
        </a>
        . Recharging in 15 Minutes to 80 Percent
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ShanghaiExpo2010_Shuttle_Bus.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/ShanghaiExpo2010_Shuttle_Bus.jpg/220px-ShanghaiExpo2010_Shuttle_Bus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/ShanghaiExpo2010_Shuttle_Bus.jpg/330px-ShanghaiExpo2010_Shuttle_Bus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/ShanghaiExpo2010_Shuttle_Bus.jpg/440px-ShanghaiExpo2010_Shuttle_Bus.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ShanghaiExpo2010_Shuttle_Bus.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BYD_electric_bus" title="BYD electric bus">
         BYD electric bus
        </a>
        in Shanghai at a charging station
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TOSA_Aeroport_rail_avec_t%C3%AAte.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2304" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/TOSA_Aeroport_rail_avec_t%C3%AAte.JPG/220px-TOSA_Aeroport_rail_avec_t%C3%AAte.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/TOSA_Aeroport_rail_avec_t%C3%AAte.JPG/330px-TOSA_Aeroport_rail_avec_t%C3%AAte.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/TOSA_Aeroport_rail_avec_t%C3%AAte.JPG/440px-TOSA_Aeroport_rail_avec_t%C3%AAte.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TOSA_Aeroport_rail_avec_t%C3%AAte.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A
        <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_bus" title="Battery electric bus">
         battery electric bus
        </a>
        charging station in Geneva, Swiss
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Charging_station" title="Charging station">
       Charging station
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      EVs typically charge from conventional power outlets or dedicated charging stations, a process that typically takes hours, but can be done overnight and often gives a charge that is sufficient for normal everyday usage.
     </p>
     <p>
      However, with the widespread implementation of
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_network" title="Electric vehicle network">
       electric vehicle networks
      </a>
      within large cities, such as those provided by POD Point
      <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.pod-point.com/" rel="nofollow">
       [1]
      </a>
      in the UK and Europe, EV users can plug in their cars whilst at work and leave them to charge throughout the day, extending the possible range of commutes and eliminating
      <a href="/wiki/Range_anxiety" title="Range anxiety">
       range anxiety
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      A recharging system that avoids the need for a cable is Curb Connect, patented in 2012
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        [64]
       </a>
      </sup>
      by Dr Gordon Dower. In this system, electrical contacts are fitted into curbs, such as angle parking spaces on city streets. When a suitably authorized vehicle is parked so that its front end overhangs the curb, the curb contacts become energized and charging occurs.
     </p>
     <p>
      Another proposed solution for daily recharging is a standardized
      <a href="/wiki/Inductive_charging" title="Inductive charging">
       inductive charging
      </a>
      system such as Evatran's
      <a href="/wiki/Plugless_Power" title="Plugless Power">
       Plugless Power
      </a>
      . Benefits are the convenience of parking over the charge station and minimized cabling and connection infrastructure.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cleantech100120_65-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cleantech100120-65">
        [65]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swvatoday090918_66-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-swvatoday090918-66">
        [66]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bnet100226_67-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bnet100226-67">
        [67]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">
       Qualcomm
      </a>
      is trialling such a system in London in early 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        [68]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        [69]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Yet another proposed solution for the typically less frequent, long distance travel is "rapid charging", such as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aerovironment" title="Aerovironment">
       Aerovironment
      </a>
      PosiCharge line (up to 250 kW) and the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Norvik&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Norvik (page does not exist)">
       Norvik
      </a>
      MinitCharge line (up to 300 kW).
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ecotality&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ecotality (page does not exist)">
       Ecotality
      </a>
      is a manufacturer of Charging Stations and has partnered with Nissan on several installations. Battery replacement is also proposed as an alternative, although no OEMs including Nissan/Renault have any production vehicle plans. Swapping requires standardization across platforms, models and manufacturers. Swapping also requires many times more battery packs to be in the system.
     </p>
     <p>
      One type of battery "replacement" proposed,
      <a href="/wiki/Vanadium_redox_battery" title="Vanadium redox battery">
       vanadium redox battery
      </a>
      , is much simpler: while the latest generation of
      <a href="/wiki/Vanadium_redox_battery" title="Vanadium redox battery">
       vanadium redox battery
      </a>
      only has an energy density similar to lead-acid, the charge is stored solely in a vanadium-based electrolyte, which can be pumped out and replaced with charged fluid
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      . The vanadium battery system is also a potential candidate for intermediate energy storage in quick charging stations because of its high power density and extremely good endurance in daily use
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      . System cost however, is still prohibitive. As vanadium battery systems are estimated to range between $350–$600 per kWh, a battery that can service one hundred customers in a 24-hour period at 50 kWh per charge would cost $1.8-$3 million
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      According to
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">
       Department of Energy
      </a>
      research conducted at
      <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest_National_Laboratory" title="Pacific Northwest National Laboratory">
       Pacific Northwest National Laboratory
      </a>
      , 84% of existing vehicles could be switched over to
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">
       plug-in hybrids
      </a>
      without requiring any new grid infrastructure.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        [70]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In terms of transportation, the net result would be a 27% total reduction in emissions of the
      <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">
       greenhouse gases
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">
       carbon dioxide
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">
       methane
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Nitrous_oxide" title="Nitrous oxide">
       nitrous oxide
      </a>
      , a 31% total reduction in
      <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">
       nitrogen oxides
      </a>
      , a slight reduction in nitrous oxide emissions, an increase in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmospheric_particulate_matter" title="Atmospheric particulate matter">
       particulate matter
      </a>
      emissions, the same
      <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">
       sulfur dioxide
      </a>
      emissions, and the near elimination of
      <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide" title="Carbon monoxide">
       carbon monoxide
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Volatile_organic_compound" title="Volatile organic compound">
       volatile organic compound
      </a>
      emissions (a 98% decrease in carbon monoxide and a 93% decrease in volatile organic compounds).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        [71]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The emissions would be displaced away from street level, where they have "high human-health implications."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        [72]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Battery_swapping">
       Battery swapping
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Battery swapping">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Instead of recharging EVs from electric socket, batteries could be mechanically replaced on special stations in a couple of minutes (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battery_swapping" title="Battery swapping">
       battery swapping
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      Batteries with greatest
      <a href="/wiki/Energy_density" title="Energy density">
       energy density
      </a>
      such as metal-air fuel cells usually cannot be recharged in purely electric way. Instead, some kind of metallurgical process is needed, such as aluminum smelting and similar.
     </p>
     <p>
      Silicon-air, aluminum-air and other metal-air fuel cells look promising candidates for swap batteries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        [73]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        [74]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Any source of energy, renewable or non-renewable, could be used to remake used metal-air fuel cells with relatively high efficiency. Investment in infrastructure will be needed. The cost of such batteries could be an issue, although they could be made with replaceable anodes and electrolyte.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Chassis_swapping">
       Chassis swapping
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Chassis swapping">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Instead of replacing batteries, it is possible to replace the entire chassis (including the batteries, electric motor and wheels) of an electric
      <a href="/wiki/Modular_vehicle" title="Modular vehicle">
       Modular vehicle
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Such a system was patented in 2000
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        [75]
       </a>
      </sup>
      by Dr Gordon Dower and three road-licensed prototypes have been built by the
      <a class="external text" href="http://ridek.com" rel="nofollow">
       Ridek Corporation
      </a>
      in Point Roberts, Washington.
     </p>
     <p>
      Dr Dower has proposed that an individual might own only the body (or perhaps a few different style bodies) for their vehicle, and would lease the chassis from a pool, thereby reducing the depreciation costs associated with vehicle ownership.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_in-development_technologies">
       Other in-development technologies
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Other in-development technologies">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_double-layer_capacitor" title="Electric double-layer capacitor">
       Electric double-layer capacitor
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Conventional
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_double-layer_capacitor" title="Electric double-layer capacitor">
       electric double-layer capacitors
      </a>
      are being worked to achieve the energy density of lithium ion batteries, offering almost unlimited lifespans and no environmental issues. High-K electric double-layer capacitors, such as
      <a href="/wiki/EEStor" title="EEStor">
       EEStor
      </a>
      's EESU, could improve lithium ion energy density several times over if they can be produced. Lithium-sulphur batteries offer
      <span class="nowrap">
       250 Wh/kg
      </span>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        [76]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sodium-ion batteries promise
      <span class="nowrap">
       400 Wh/kg
      </span>
      with only minimal expansion/contraction during charge/discharge and a very high surface area.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        [77]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Researchers from one of the Ukrainian state universities claim that they have manufactured samples of pseudocapacitor based on Li-ion intercalation process with
      <span class="nowrap">
       318 Wh/kg
      </span>
      specific energy, which seem to be at least two times improvement in comparison to typical Li-ion batteries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        [78]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">
       Safety
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Safety">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
       United Nations
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">
       Geneva
      </a>
      (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNECE" title="UNECE">
       UNECE
      </a>
      ) has adopted the first international regulation (Regulation 100) on safety of both fully electric and hybrid electric cars, with the intent of ensuring that cars with a
      <a href="/wiki/High_voltage" title="High voltage">
       high voltage
      </a>
      electric power train, such as hybrid and fully EVs, are as safe as
      <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">
       combustion-powered
      </a>
      cars. The EU and Japan have already indicated that they intend to incorporate the new UNECE Regulation in their respective rules on technical standards for vehicles
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        [79]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      There is a growing concern about the safety of EVs, given the demonstrated tendency of the Lithium-ion battery, most promising for EV use because of its high energy density, to overheat, possibly leading to fire or explosion, especially when damaged in a crash. The U.S.
      <a href="/wiki/National_Highway_Traffic_Safety_Administration" title="National Highway Traffic Safety Administration">
       National Highway Traffic Safety Administration
      </a>
      opened a defect investigation of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chevy_Volt" title="Chevy Volt">
       Chevy Volt
      </a>
      on November 25, 2011 amid concerns over the risk of battery fires in a crash. At that time, automotive consulting firm
      <a href="/wiki/CNW_Marketing_Research" title="CNW Marketing Research">
       CNW Marketing Research
      </a>
      reported a decline in consumer interest in the Volt, citing the fires as having made an impact on consumer perception.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        [80]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Consumer response impelled GM to make safety enhancements to the battery system in December, and the NHTSA closed its investigation on January 20, 2012, finding the matter satisfactorily resolved with "no discernible defect trend" remaining. The agency also announced it has developed interim guidance to increase awareness and identify appropriate safety measures regarding electric vehicles for the emergency response community, law enforcement officers, tow truck operators, storage facilities and consumers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NTHSAfind01_81-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NTHSAfind01-81">
        [81]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NTHSAfind02_82-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NTHSAfind02-82">
        [82]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Advantages_and_disadvantages_of_EVs">
       Advantages and disadvantages of EVs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Advantages and disadvantages of EVs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;width:18.0em;">

     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental">
       Environmental
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Environmental">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      EVs release no tail pipe air pollutants at the place where they are operated. They also typically generate less
      <a href="/wiki/Noise_pollution" title="Noise pollution">
       noise pollution
      </a>
      than an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine_vehicle" title="Internal combustion engine vehicle">
       internal combustion engine vehicle
      </a>
      , whether at rest or in motion.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ec.europa.eu_83-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ec.europa.eu-83">
        [83]
       </a>
      </sup>
      The energy that electric and hybrid cars consume is usually
      <a href="/wiki/Electricity_generation" title="Electricity generation">
       generated
      </a>
      by means that have environmental impacts. Nevertheless, adaptation of EVs would have a significant net environmental benefit, except in a few countries that continue to rely on older coal fired power plants for the bulk of their electricity generation throughout the life of the car.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        [84]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Buekers_85-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Buekers-85">
        [85]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        [86]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      There are special kind of electric vehicles named SAFA TEMPO in Nepal that help lower the pollution created by vehicles.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        [87]
       </a>
      </sup>
      These vehicles are powered by electricity - usually charged batteries - rather than oil or gas and currently heavily promoted by the government to facilitate environmental and vehicle management issues.. Electric motors don't require oxygen, unlike
      <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">
       internal combustion engines
      </a>
      ; this is useful for
      <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">
       submarines
      </a>
      and for
      <a href="/wiki/Rover_(space_exploration)" title="Rover (space exploration)">
       space rovers
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Mechanical">
       Mechanical
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Mechanical">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1431" data-file-width="2153" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG/220px-Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG/330px-Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG/440px-Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Motors_Model_S_base.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">
         Tesla Model S
        </a>
        chassis with drive motor
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg/220px-Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg/330px-Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg/440px-Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tesla_Model_S_motor_cutout.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Cutaway view of a
        <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">
         Tesla Model S
        </a>
        drive motor
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Electric motors are mechanically very simple and often achieve 90%
      <a href="/wiki/Energy_conversion_efficiency" title="Energy conversion efficiency">
       energy conversion efficiency
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        [88]
       </a>
      </sup>
      over the full range of speeds and power output and can be precisely controlled. They can also be combined with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking">
       regenerative braking
      </a>
      systems that have the ability to convert movement energy back into stored electricity. This can be used to reduce the wear on brake systems (and consequent brake pad dust) and reduce the total energy requirement of a trip. Regenerative braking is especially effective for start-and-stop city use.
     </p>
     <p>
      They can be finely controlled and provide high torque from rest, unlike
      <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">
       internal combustion engines
      </a>
      , and do not need multiple gears to match power curves. This removes the need for
      <a href="/wiki/Transmission_(mechanics)" title="Transmission (mechanics)">
       gearboxes
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Torque_converter" title="Torque converter">
       torque converters
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      EVs provide quiet and smooth operation and consequently have less noise and
      <a href="/wiki/Vibration" title="Vibration">
       vibration
      </a>
      than internal combustion engines.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ec.europa.eu_83-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-ec.europa.eu-83">
        [83]
       </a>
      </sup>
      While this is a desirable attribute, it has also evoked concern that the absence of the usual sounds of an approaching vehicle poses a danger to blind, elderly and very young pedestrians. To mitigate this situation, automakers and individual companies are developing systems that produce
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_vehicle_warning_sounds" title="Electric vehicle warning sounds">
       warning sounds
      </a>
      when EVs are moving slowly, up to a speed when normal motion and rotation (road, suspension, electric motor, etc.) noises become audible.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        [89]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_resilience">
       Energy resilience
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Energy resilience">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Electricity can be produced from a variety of sources, therefore it gives the greatest degree of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_resilience" title="Energy resilience">
       energy resilience
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        [90]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy_efficiency">
       Energy efficiency
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Energy efficiency">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      EV '
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tank-to-wheel" title="Tank-to-wheel">
       tank-to-wheels
      </a>
      ' efficiency is about a factor of 3 higher than
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine_vehicle" title="Internal combustion engine vehicle">
       internal combustion engine vehicles
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ec.europa.eu_83-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-ec.europa.eu-83">
        [83]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Energy is not consumed while the vehicle is stationary, unlike internal combustion engines which consume fuel while idling. However, looking at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Well-to-wheel" title="Well-to-wheel">
       well-to-wheel
      </a>
      efficiency of EVs, their total emissions, while still lower, are closer to an efficient gasoline or diesel in most countries where electricity generation relies on fossil fuels.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        [91]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UCS2015_92-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-UCS2015-92">
        [92]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        [93]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Well-to-wheel efficiency of an EV has less to do with the vehicle itself and more to do with the method of electricity production. A particular EV would instantly become twice as efficient if electricity production were switched from fossil fuel to a wind or tidal primary source of energy. Thus, when "well-to-wheels" is cited, one should keep in mind that the discussion is no longer about the vehicle, but rather about the entire energy supply infrastructure - in the case of fossil fuels this should also include energy spent on exploration, mining, refining, and distribution.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cost_of_recharge">
       Cost of recharge
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Cost of recharge">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      According to General Motors, as reported by CNN Money, the GM Volt will cost "less than purchasing a cup of your favorite coffee" to recharge. The Volt should cost less than 2 cents per mile to drive on electricity, compared with 12 cents a mile on gasoline at a price of $3.60 a gallon. This means a trip from Los Angeles to New York would cost $56 on electricity, and $336 with gasoline. This would be the equivalent to paying 60 cents a gallon of gas.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        [94]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The reality is that the cost of operating an EV varies wildly depending on the part of the world in which the owner lives. In some locations an EV costs less to drive than a comparable gas-powered vehicle, as long as the higher initial purchase-price is not factored in (i.e. a pure comparison of gasoline cost to electricity cost). In the USA, however, in states which have a tiered electricity rate schedule, "fuel" for EVs today costs owners significantly more than fuel for a comparable gas-powered vehicle. A study done by Purdue University found that in California most users already reach the third pricing tier for electricity each month, and adding an EV could push them into the fourth or fifth (highest, most expensive) tier, meaning that they will be paying in excess of $.45 cents per KWH for electricity to recharge their vehicle. At this price, which is higher than the average electricity price in the US, it is dramatically more expensive to drive a pure-EV than it is to drive a traditional pure-gas powered vehicle. "The objective of a tiered pricing system is to discourage consumption. It's meant to get you to think about turning off your lights and conserving electricity. In California, the unintended consequence is that plug-in hybrid cars won't be economical under this system," said Tyner (the author), whose findings were published in the online version of the journal Energy Policy.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        [95]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Stabilization_of_the_grid">
       Stabilization of the grid
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Stabilization of the grid">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Since EVs can be plugged into the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_grid" title="Electric grid">
       electric grid
      </a>
      when not in use, there is a potential for battery powered vehicles to even cut the demand for electricity by feeding electricity
      <i>
       into
      </i>
      the grid from their batteries during peak use periods (such as midafternoon air conditioning use) while doing most of their charging at night, when there is unused generating capacity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        [96]
       </a>
      </sup>
      This
      <a href="/wiki/Vehicle-to-grid" title="Vehicle-to-grid">
       vehicle-to-grid
      </a>
      (V2G) connection has the potential to reduce the need for new power plants, as long as vehicle owners do not mind reducing the life of their batteries, by being drained by the power company during peak demand.
     </p>
     <p>
      Furthermore, our current electricity infrastructure may need to cope with increasing shares of variable-output power sources such as windmills and PV solar panels. This variability could be addressed by adjusting the speed at which EV batteries are charged, or possibly even discharged.
     </p>
     <p>
      Some concepts see battery exchanges and battery charging stations, much like gas/petrol stations today. Clearly these will require enormous storage and charging potentials, which could be manipulated to vary the rate of charging, and to output power during shortage periods, much as diesel generators are used for short periods to stabilize some national grids.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        [97]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        [98]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Range">
       Range
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Range">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      Many electric designs have limited range, due to the low energy density of batteries compared to the fuel of internal combustion engined vehicles. EVs also often have long recharge times compared to the relatively fast process of refueling a tank. This is further complicated by the current scarcity of public charging stations. "
      <a href="/wiki/Range_anxiety" title="Range anxiety">
       Range anxiety
      </a>
      " is a label for consumer concern about EV range.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Heating_of_EVs">
       Heating of EVs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Heating of EVs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      In cold climates, considerable energy is needed to heat the interior of a vehicle and to defrost the windows. With internal combustion engines, this heat already exists as waste combustion heat diverted from the engine cooling circuit. This process offsets the
      <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">
       greenhouse gases
      </a>
      ' external costs. If this is done with battery EVs, the interior heating requires extra energy from the vehicles' batteries. Although some heat could be harvested from the motor or motors and battery, their greater efficiency means there is not as much waste heat available as from a
      <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">
       combustion engine
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      However, for vehicles which are connected to the grid, battery EVs can be preheated, or cooled, with little or no need for battery energy, especially for short trips.
     </p>
     <p>
      Newer designs are focused on using super-
      <a href="/wiki/Thermal_insulation" title="Thermal insulation">
       insulated
      </a>
      cabins which can heat the vehicle using the body heat of the passengers. This is not enough, however, in colder climates as a driver delivers only about 100 W of heating power. A
      <a href="/wiki/Heat_pump" title="Heat pump">
       heat pump
      </a>
      system, capable of cooling the cabin during summer and heating it during winter, seems to be the most practical and promising way of solving the thermal management of the EV. Ricardo Arboix
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        [99]
       </a>
      </sup>
      introduced (2008) a new concept based on the principle of combining the thermal-management of the EV-battery with the thermal-management of the cabin using a heat pump system. This is done by adding a third heat-exchanger, thermally connected with the battery-core, to the traditional heat pump/air conditioning system used in previous EV-models like the GM EV1 and Toyota RAV4 EV. The concept has proven to bring several benefits, such as prolonging the life-span of the battery as well as improving the performance and overall energy-efficiency of the EV.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        [100]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        [101]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        [102]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        [103]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Electric_public_transit_efficiency">
       Electric public transit efficiency
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Electric public transit efficiency">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Shifts from private to
      <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">
       public transport
      </a>
      (train,
      <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">
       trolleybus
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Personal_rapid_transit" title="Personal rapid transit">
       personal rapid transit
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">
       tram
      </a>
      ) have the potential for large gains in efficiency in terms of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Individual_mile_per_kWH&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Individual mile per kWH (page does not exist)">
       individual miles per kWh
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Research shows people do prefer trams,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        [104]
       </a>
      </sup>
      because they are quieter and more comfortable and perceived as having higher status.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        [105]
       </a>
      </sup>
      Therefore, it may be possible to cut liquid fossil fuel consumption in cities through the use of electric trams. Trams may be the most energy-efficient form of public transportation, with rubber wheeled vehicles using 2/3 more energy than the equivalent tram, and run on electricity rather than fossil fuels.
     </p>
     <p>
      In terms of
      <a href="/wiki/Net_present_value" title="Net present value">
       net present value
      </a>
      , they are also the cheapest—
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blackpool_tram" title="Blackpool tram">
       Blackpool trams
      </a>
      are still running after 100-years,
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      but combustion buses only last about 15-years.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Incentives_and_promotion">
       Incentives and promotion
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Incentives and promotion">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Government_incentives_for_plug-in_electric_vehicles" title="Government incentives for plug-in electric vehicles">
       Government incentives for plug-in electric vehicles
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_car_use_by_country" title="Electric car use by country">
       Electric car use by country
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Many governments offer incentives to promote the use of electric vehicles, with the goals of reducing air pollution and oil consumption. Some incentives intend to increase purchases of electric vehicles by offsetting the purchase price with a grant. Other incentives include lower tax rates or exemption from certain taxes, and investment in charging infrastructure.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Future">
       Future
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Future">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_electric_vehicle" title="Plug-in electric vehicle">
       Plug-in electric vehicle
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Battery_electric_vehicle" title="Battery electric vehicle">
       Battery electric vehicle
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Plug-in_hybrid" title="Plug-in hybrid">
       Plug-in hybrid
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Salon_Priv%C3%A9_London_2012_(7956529248).jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2304" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Salon_Priv%C3%A9_London_2012_%287956529248%29.jpg/220px-Salon_Priv%C3%A9_London_2012_%287956529248%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Salon_Priv%C3%A9_London_2012_%287956529248%29.jpg/330px-Salon_Priv%C3%A9_London_2012_%287956529248%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Salon_Priv%C3%A9_London_2012_%287956529248%29.jpg/440px-Salon_Priv%C3%A9_London_2012_%287956529248%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Salon_Priv%C3%A9_London_2012_(7956529248).jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Rimac_Concept_One" title="Rimac Concept One">
         Rimac Concept One
        </a>
        , electric supercar, since 2013. 0 to 100 km/h in 2.8 seconds, 1088 hp
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2013_Tesla_Model_S_(11322176214)_cropped.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="753" data-file-width="1200" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/2013_Tesla_Model_S_%2811322176214%29_cropped.jpg/220px-2013_Tesla_Model_S_%2811322176214%29_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/2013_Tesla_Model_S_%2811322176214%29_cropped.jpg/330px-2013_Tesla_Model_S_%2811322176214%29_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/2013_Tesla_Model_S_%2811322176214%29_cropped.jpg/440px-2013_Tesla_Model_S_%2811322176214%29_cropped.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2013_Tesla_Model_S_(11322176214)_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Model_S" title="Tesla Model S">
         Tesla Model S
        </a>
        , since 2012. 0 to 100 km/h in 2.5 seconds, recharging in 30 minutes to 80 percent, range 600 km
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Ferdinand Dudenhoeffer, head of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centre_of_Automotive_Research" title="Centre of Automotive Research">
       Centre of Automotive Research
      </a>
      at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gelsenkirchen_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Gelsenkirchen University of Applied Sciences">
       Gelsenkirchen University of Applied Sciences
      </a>
      in Germany, said that "by 2025, all
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile" title="Automobile">
       passenger cars
      </a>
      sold in Europe will be electric or hybrid electric".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-euobserver.com_106-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-euobserver.com-106">
        [106]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Improved_batteries">
       Improved batteries
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Improved batteries">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      First, advances in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithium_ion_battery" title="Lithium ion battery">
       lithium ion batteries
      </a>
      , in large part driven by the consumer electronics industry, allow full-sized, highway-capable EVs to be propelled as far on a single charge as conventional cars go on a single tank of gasoline. Lithium batteries have been made safe, can be recharged in minutes instead of hours (see
      <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery#Recharging_time" title="Rechargeable battery">
       recharging time
      </a>
      ), and now last longer than the typical vehicle (see
      <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery#Lifespan_and_cycle_stability" title="Rechargeable battery">
       lifespan
      </a>
      ). The production cost of these lighter, higher-capacity lithium batteries is gradually decreasing as the technology matures and production volumes increase (see
      <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery#Price_history" title="Rechargeable battery">
       price history
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">
       Toyota
      </a>
      Motors Corporation is trying to replace the current lithium ion battery with
      <a href="/wiki/Solid-state_battery" title="Solid-state battery">
       solid-state battery
      </a>
      technology by 2020. The solid-state battery replaces the liquid electrolyte with a solid electrolyte.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        [107]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        [108]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Rechargeable
      <a href="/wiki/Lithium%E2%80%93air_battery" title="Lithium–air battery">
       lithium-air batteries
      </a>
      potentially offer increased range over other types and are a current topic of research.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        [109]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Battery_management_and_intermediate_storage">
       Battery management and intermediate storage
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Battery management and intermediate storage">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Another improvement is to decouple the electric motor from the battery through electronic control, employing
      <a href="/wiki/Supercapacitor" title="Supercapacitor">
       supercapacitors
      </a>
      to buffer large but short power demands and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regenerative_braking" title="Regenerative braking">
       regenerative braking
      </a>
      energy. The development of new cell types combined with intelligent cell management improved both weak points mentioned above. The cell management involves not only monitoring the health of the cells but also a redundant cell configuration (one more cell than needed). With sophisticated switched wiring it is possible to condition one cell while the rest are on duty.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="EV_organizations">
       EV organizations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: EV organizations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Worldwide">
       Worldwide
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Electric_vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Worldwide">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/World_Electric_Vehicle_Association" title="World Electric Vehicle Association">
        World Electric Vehicle Association
       </a>
       (WEVA),
       <a href="/wiki/Chairman" title="Chairman">
        chairman
       </a>
       Hisashi Ishitani, formed by:
      </li>
      <li>
       Electric Drive Transportation Association (EDTA)
      </li>
      <li>
       Electric Vehicle Association of Asia Pacific (EVAAP)
      </li>
      <li>
       European Association for Battery, Hybrid and Fuel Cell Electric Vehicles (AVERE)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Multilateral_Cooperation_to_Advance_Electric_Vehicles&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Multilateral Cooperation to Advance Electric Vehicles (page does not exist)">
        Multilateral Cooperation to Advance Electric Vehicles
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       The Implementing Agreement for co-operation on Hybrid and Electric Vehicle Technologies and Programmes (A-HEV) - IA-HEV was formed in 1993 to produce and disseminate balanced, objective information about advanced electric, hybrid, and fuel cell vehicles. IA-HEV is an international membership group collaborating under the International Energy Agency (IEA) framework.
      </li>
     </ul>

           </a>

          , cumulative global sales of the top selling plug-in electric cars were led by the Nissan Leaf (over 228,000), followed by theTesla Model S (129,393), Votl/Ampera family (about 117,300), Mitsubishi Outlander PHEV (about 107,400), Toyota Prius PHV (over 75,400), BYD Qin (56,191), Renault Zoe (51,193), BMW i3 (around 49,500), Mitsubishi i-MiEV family (about 37,600) and BYD Tang (37,509).
